       After word splitting, unless the [1m-f[0m option has been set,  [1mbash[0m[m
       scans  each  word  for  the characters [1m*[0m, [1m?[0m, and [1m[[0m.  If one of[m
       these characters appears, and is not quoted, then the word  is[m
       regarded  as  a  [4mpattern[24m,  and replaced with an alphabetically[m
       sorted list of filenames matching  the  pattern  (see  [1mPattern[0m[m
       [1mMatching[0m  below).  If no matching filenames are found, and the[m
       shell option [1mnullglob[0m is not enabled, the  word  is  left  un‚Äê[m
       changed.   If  the  [1mnullglob[0m option is set, and no matches are[m
       found, the word is removed.  If the [1mfailglob[0m shell  option  is[m
       set, and no matches are found, an error message is printed and[m
       the command is not executed.  If the shell  option  [1mnocaseglob[0m[m
       is  enabled, the match is performed without regard to the case[m
       of alphabetic characters.  Note that when using range  expres‚Äê[m
       sions like [a-z] (see below), letters of the other case may be[m
       included, depending on the setting of [1mLC_COLLATE.[0m  When a pat‚Äê[m
       tern  is  used for pathname expansion, the character [1m``.''[0m  at[m

   [1m[7mPathname[27m[0m[7m [27m[1m[7mExpansion[27m[0m[m
       After word splitting, unless the [1m-f[0m option has been set,  [1mbash[0m[m
       scans  each  word  for  the characters [1m*[0m, [1m?[0m, and [1m[[0m.  If one of[m
       these characters appears, and is not quoted, then the word  is[m
       regarded  as  a  [4mpattern[24m,  and replaced with an alphabetically[m
       sorted list of filenames matching  the  pattern  (see  [1mPattern[0m[m
       [1mMatching[0m  below).  If no matching filenames are found, and the[m
       shell option [1mnullglob[0m is not enabled, the  word  is  left  un‚Äê[m
       changed.   If  the  [1mnullglob[0m option is set, and no matches are[m
       found, the word is removed.  If the [1mfailglob[0m shell  option  is[m
       set, and no matches are found, an error message is printed and[m
       the command is not executed.  If the shell  option  [1mnocaseglob[0m[m
       is  enabled, the match is performed without regard to the case[m

       described  below  under  [1mTilde[0m [1mExpansion[0m in the [1m[7mEXPANSION[27m[0m sec‚Äê[m
       tion.[m
[m
       When [1mbash[0m is invoked as an interactive login shell,  or  as  a[m
       non-interactive  shell with the [1m--login[0m option, it first reads[m
       and executes commands from the file [4m/etc/profile[24m, if that file[m
       exists.   After  reading  that file, it looks for [4m~/.bash_pro‚Äê[24m[m
       [4mfile[24m, [4m~/.bash_login[24m, and [4m~/.profile[24m, in that order, and  reads[m
       and  executes  commands  from the first one that exists and is[m
       readable.  The [1m--noprofile[0m option may be used when  the  shell[m
       is started to inhibit this behavior.[m
[m
       When  an  interactive  login shell exits, or a non-interactive[m
       login shell executes the [1mexit[0m builtin command, [1mbash[0m reads  and[m
       executes commands from the file [4m~/.bash_logout[24m, if it exists.[m
[m
       When  an  interactive  shell  that  is  not  a  login shell is[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 160/7447 2% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K...skipping...
       (see [1mHISTORY[0m [1m[7mEXPANSION[27m[0m below), the [4mhistory[24m  [4mexpansion[24m  charac‚Äê[m
       ter, usually [1m![0m, must be quoted to prevent history expansion.[m
[m
       There are three quoting mechanisms: the [4mescape[24m [4mcharacter[24m, sin‚Äê[m
       gle quotes, and double quotes.[m
[m
       A non-quoted backslash ([1m\[0m) is the [4mescape[24m [4mcharacter[24m.   It  pre‚Äê[m
       serves  the  literal value of the next character that follows,[m
       with the exception of <newline>.  If  a  [1m\[0m<newline>  pair  ap‚Äê[m
       pears,  and the backslash is not itself quoted, the [1m\[0m<newline>[m
       is treated as a line continuation (that is, it is removed from[m
       the input stream and effectively ignored).[m
[m
       Enclosing  characters  in  single quotes preserves the literal[m
       value of each character within the quotes.  A single quote may[m
       not occur between single quotes, even when preceded by a back‚Äê[m
       slash.[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 686/7447 9% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K...skipping...
       sion,  and  quote removal (see [1m[7mEXPANSION[27m[0m below).  If the vari‚Äê[m
       able has its [1minteger[0m attribute set, then [4mvalue[24m is evaluated as[m
       an arithmetic expression even if the $((...)) expansion is not[m
       used (see [1mArithmetic[0m [1mExpansion[0m  below).   Word  splitting  and[m

[m
       In the context where an assignment statement  is  assigning  a[m

       This  includes  arguments  to builtin commands such as [1mdeclare[0m[m

[7mManual page bash(1) line 789/7447 11% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K...skipping...
              pansion and tokenization (see [1mHISTORY[0m [1m[7mEXPANSION[27m[0m below).[m
              The first character is the [4mhistory[24m [4mexpansion[24m character,[m
              the character which signals the start of a history  ex‚Äê[m
              pansion,  normally  `[1m![0m'.   The  second character is the[m
              [4mquick[24m [4msubstitution[24m character, which is used  as  short‚Äê[m

              default  is  `[1m^[0m'.   The optional third character is the[m

   [1mArrays[0m[m
[7manual page bash(1) line 1632/7447 23% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K...skipping...
       all  the  shell  expansions  described  below under [1m[7mEXPANSION[27m[0m.[m
       When assigning to indexed arrays, if the optional brackets and[m
       subscript  are  supplied, that index is assigned to; otherwise[m
       the index of the element assigned is the last  index  assigned[m
       to by the statement plus one.  Indexing starts at zero.[m
[m
       When  assigning  to  an associative array, the words in a com‚Äê[m
       pound assignment may  be  either  assignment  statements,  for[m
       which  the  subscript  is required, or a list of words that is[m
       interpreted as a sequence  of  alternating  keys  and  values:[m
       [4mname[24m=[1m([0m  [4mkey1[24m [4mvalue1[24m [4mkey2[24m [4mvalue2[24m ...[1m)[0m.  These are treated iden‚Äê[m

       word in the list determines how the remaining words are inter‚Äê[m
       preted; all assignments in a list must be of  the  same  type.[m
       When  using  key/value  pairs,  the keys may not be missing or[m
       empty; a final missing value is treated like the empty string.[m

[1m[7mEXPANSION[27m[0m[m
       Expansion is performed on the command line after it  has  been[m
       split  into  words.   There  are seven kinds of expansion per‚Äê[m
       formed: [4mbrace[24m [4mexpansion[24m, [4mtilde[24m [4mexpansion[24m, [4mparameter[24m [4mand[24m  [4mvari‚Äê[24m[m
       [4mable[24m  [4mexpansion[24m,  [4mcommand[24m  [4msubstitution[24m, [4marithmetic[24m [4mexpansion[24m,[m
       [4mword[24m [4msplitting[24m, and [4mpathname[24m [4mexpansion[24m.[m
[m
       The order of expansions is: brace expansion; tilde  expansion,[m
       parameter  and  variable  expansion, arithmetic expansion, and[m
       command substitution (done in a left-to-right  fashion);  word[m
       splitting; and pathname expansion.[m
[m
       On  systems that can support it, there is an additional expan‚Äê[m
       sion available: [4mprocess[24m [4msubstitution[24m.  This  is  performed  at[m
       the  same  time  as tilde, parameter, variable, and arithmetic[m
       expansion and command substitution.[m

[17;1H       [1m>([0m[4mlist[24m[1m)[0m.  The process [4mlist[24m is run asynchronously, and its  in‚Äê[m
[18;1H[1;1H       The  [4mexpression[24m  undergoes  the  same expansions as if it were[m
[2;1H       within double quotes, but double quote characters  in  [4mexpres‚Äê[24m[m
[3;1H       [4msion[24m are not treated specially and are removed.  All tokens in[m
[4;1H       the expression undergo parameter and variable expansion,  com‚Äê[m
[5;1H       mand  substitution,  and quote removal.  The result is treated[m
[6;1H       as the arithmetic expression to be evaluated.  Arithmetic  ex‚Äê[m
[7;1H       pansions may be nested.[m
[8;1H[m
[9;1H       The  evaluation is performed according to the rules listed be‚Äê[m
[10;1H       low under [1m[7mARITHMETIC[27m[0m[7m [27m[1m[7mEVALUATION[27m[0m.  If  [4mexpression[24m  is  invalid,[m
[11;1H       [1mbash[0m  prints  a message indicating failure and no substitution[m
[12;1H       occurs.[m
[13;1H[m
[14;1H   [1mProcess[0m [1mSubstitution[0m[m
[15;1H       [4mProcess[24m [4msubstitution[24m allows a process's input or output to  be[m
[16;1H       referred to using a filename.  It takes the form of [1m<([0m[4mlist[24m[1m)[0m or[m
[17;1H       [1m>([0m[4mlist[24m[1m)[0m.  The process [4mlist[24m is run asynchronously, and its  in‚Äê[m
[18;1H       put  or output appears as a filename.  This filename is passed[m
       as an argument to the current command as the result of the ex‚Äê[m
       pansion.   If  the  [1m>([0m[4mlist[24m[1m)[0m  form is used, writing to the file[m
       will provide input for [4mlist[24m.  If the [1m<([0m[4mlist[24m[1m)[0m form is used, the[m
       file passed as an argument should be read to obtain the output[m
       of [4mlist[24m.  Process substitution is supported  on  systems  that[m
       support  named  pipes  ([4mFIFOs[24m) or the [1m/dev/fd[0m method of naming[m
       open files.[m

[1m[7mARITHMETIC[27m[0m[7m [27m[1m[7mEVALUATION[27m[0m[m
       The shell allows arithmetic expressions to be evaluated, under[m
       certain  circumstances  (see  the [1mlet[0m and [1mdeclare[0m builtin com‚Äê[m
       mands, the [1m(([0m compound  command,  and  [1mArithmetic[0m  [1mExpansion[0m).[m
       Evaluation  is  done in fixed-width integers with no check for[m
       overflow, though division by 0 is trapped and  flagged  as  an[m
       error.  The operators and their precedence, associativity, and[m
       values are the same as in the C language.  The following  list[m
       of operators is grouped into levels of equal-precedence opera‚Äê[m
       tors.  The levels are listed in  order  of  decreasing  prece‚Äê[m
       dence.[m
[m

       [1m++[0m[4mid[24m [1m--[0m[4mid[24m[m

       [1mBash[0m is an [1msh[0m-compatible command language interpreter that ex‚Äê[m
       ecutes  commands  read from the standard input or from a file.[m
       [1mBash[0m also incorporates useful features from  the  [4mKorn[24m  and  [4mC[24m[m
       shells ([1mksh[0m and [1mcsh[0m).[m
[m
       [1mBash[0m  is  intended  to  be  a conformant implementation of the[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       Shell and Utilities portion of the  IEEE  POSIX  specification[m
       (IEEE  Standard  1003.1).  [1mBash[0m can be configured to be POSIX-[m
       conformant by default.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       All of the single-character shell options  documented  in  the[m
       description  of  the [1mset[0m builtin command, including [1m-o[0m, can be[m
       used as options when the shell is invoked.  In addition,  [1mbash[0m[m
       interprets the following options when it is invoked:[m
[m
       [1m-c[0m        If  the [1m-c[0m option is present, then commands are read[m
                 from the first non-option  argument  [4mcommand_string[24m.[m
                 If there are arguments after the [4mcommand_string[24m, the[m
                 first argument is assigned to [1m$0[0m and  any  remaining[m
                 arguments are assigned to the positional parameters.[m
                 The assignment to [1m$0[0m sets the  name  of  the  shell,[m
                 which is used in warning and error messages.[m
       [1m-i[0m        If  the  [1m-i[0m option is present, the shell is [4minterac‚Äê[24m[m
                 [4mtive[24m.[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 20 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       [1m-l[0m        Make [1mbash[0m act as if it had been invoked as  a  login[m
                 shell (see [1mINVOCATION[0m below).[m
       [1m-r[0m        If  the  [1m-r[0m option is present, the shell becomes [4mre‚Äê[24m[m
                 [4mstricted[24m (see [1mRESTRICTED[0m [1mSHELL[0m below).[m
       [1m-s[0m        If the [1m-s[0m option is present, or if no arguments  re‚Äê[m
                 main after option processing, then commands are read[m
                 from the standard input.  This option allows the po‚Äê[m
                 sitional  parameters  to be set when invoking an in‚Äê[m
                 teractive shell or  when  reading  input  through  a[m
                 pipe.[m
       [1m-v[0m        Print shell input lines as they are read.[m
       [1m-x[0m        Print  commands and their arguments as they are exe‚Äê[m
                 cuted.[m
       [1m-D[0m        A list of all double-quoted strings preceded by [1m$[0m is[m
                 printed  on  the  standard  output.   These  are the[m
                 strings that are  subject  to  language  translation[m
                 when the current locale is not [1mC[0m or [1mPOSIX[0m.  This im‚Äê[m
                 plies the [1m-n[0m option; no commands will be executed.[m
       [1m[-+]O[0m [1m[[0m[4mshopt_option[24m[1m][0m[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 39 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K                 [4mshopt_option[24m is one of the shell options accepted by[m
                 the  [1mshopt[0m  builtin  (see [1mSHELL[0m [1mBUILTIN[0m [1mCOMMANDS[0m be‚Äê[m
                 low).  If [4mshopt_option[24m is present, [1m-O[0m sets the value[m
                 of  that  option;  [1m+O[0m unsets it.  If [4mshopt_option[24m is[m
                 not supplied, the names and values of the shell  op‚Äê[m
                 tions  accepted by [1mshopt[0m are printed on the standard[m
                 output.  If the invocation option is [1m+O[0m, the  output[m
                 is  displayed  in a format that may be reused as in‚Äê[m
                 put.[m
       [1m--[0m        A [1m--[0m signals the end of options and disables further[m
                 option  processing.   Any arguments after the [1m--[0m are[m
                 treated as filenames and arguments.  An argument  of[m
                 [1m-[0m is equivalent to [1m--[0m.[m
[m
       [1mBash[0m  also  interprets  a  number  of multi-character options.[m
       These options must appear on the command line before the  sin‚Äê[m
       gle-character options to be recognized.[m
[m
       [1m--debugger[0m[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 58 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              Arrange  for the debugger profile to be executed before[m
              the shell starts.  Turns  on  extended  debugging  mode[m
              (see  the  description  of  the  [1mextdebug[0m option to the[m
              [1mshopt[0m builtin below).[m
       [1m--dump-po-strings[0m[m
              Equivalent to [1m-D[0m, but the output is in the GNU  [4mgettext[24m[m
              [1mpo[0m (portable object) file format.[m
       [1m--dump-strings[0m[m
              Equivalent to [1m-D[0m.[m
       [1m--help[0m Display  a  usage  message  on standard output and exit[m
              successfully.[m
       [1m--init-file[0m [4mfile[24m[m
       [1m--rcfile[0m [4mfile[24m[m
              Execute commands from [4mfile[24m instead of the  system  wide[m
              initialization  file  [4m/etc/bash.bashrc[24m and the standard[m
              personal initialization file [4m~/.bashrc[24m if the shell  is[m
              interactive (see [1mINVOCATION[0m below).[m
[m
       [1m--login[0m[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 77 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              Equivalent to [1m-l[0m.[m
[m
       [1m--noediting[0m[m
              Do  not  use  the  GNU [1mreadline[0m library to read command[m
              lines when the shell is interactive.[m
[m
       [1m--noprofile[0m[m
              Do  not  read  either  the  system-wide  startup   file[m
              [4m/etc/profile[24m  or  any  of  the  personal initialization[m
              files [4m~/.bash_profile[24m,  [4m~/.bash_login[24m,  or  [4m~/.profile[24m.[m
              By  default,  [1mbash[0m reads these files when it is invoked[m
              as a login shell (see [1mINVOCATION[0m below).[m
[m
       [1m--norc[0m Do not read and execute the system wide  initialization[m
              file  [4m/etc/bash.bashrc[24m  and the personal initialization[m
              file [4m~/.bashrc[24m if the shell is interactive.   This  op‚Äê[m
              tion is on by default if the shell is invoked as [1msh[0m.[m
[m
       [1m--posix[0m[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 96 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              Change the behavior of [1mbash[0m where the default operation[m
              differs from the POSIX standard to match  the  standard[m
              ([4mposix[24m  [4mmode[24m).  See [1mSEE[0m [1mALSO[0m below for a reference to a[m
              document that details how posix mode affects bash's be‚Äê[m
              havior.[m
[m
       [1m--restricted[0m[m
              The  shell becomes restricted (see [1mRESTRICTED[0m [1mSHELL[0m be‚Äê[m
              low).[m
[m
       [1m--verbose[0m[m
              Equivalent to [1m-v[0m.[m
[m
       [1m--version[0m[m
              Show version information for this instance of  [1mbash[0m  on[m
              the standard output and exit successfully.[m
[m
[1mARGUMENTS[0m[m
       If  arguments  remain after option processing, and neither the[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 115 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       [1m-c[0m nor the [1m-s[0m option has been supplied, the first argument  is[m
       assumed  to  be  the name of a file containing shell commands.[m
       If [1mbash[0m is invoked in this fashion, [1m$0[0m is set to the  name  of[m
       the file, and the positional parameters are set to the remain‚Äê[m
       ing arguments.  [1mBash[0m reads and  executes  commands  from  this[m
       file,  then  exits.   [1mBash[0m's exit status is the exit status of[m
       the last command executed in the script.  If no  commands  are[m
       executed,  the  exit status is 0.  An attempt is first made to[m
       open the file in the current directory, and,  if  no  file  is[m
       found, then the shell searches the directories in [1mPATH[0m for the[m
       script.[m
[m
[1mINVOCATION[0m[m
       A [4mlogin[24m [4mshell[24m is one whose first character of argument zero is[m
       a [1m-[0m, or one started with the [1m--login[0m option.[m
[m
       An  [4minteractive[24m  shell is one started without non-option argu‚Äê[m
       ments (unless [1m-s[0m is specified)  and  without  the  [1m-c[0m  option,[m
       whose standard input and error are both connected to terminals[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 134 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       (as determined by [4misatty[24m(3)), or one started with the  [1m-i[0m  op‚Äê[m
       tion.   [1mPS1[0m  is  set and [1m$-[0m includes [1mi[0m if [1mbash[0m is interactive,[m
       allowing a shell script or a startup file to test this state.[m
[m
       The  following  paragraphs  describe  how  [1mbash[0m  executes  its[m
       startup  files.  If any of the files exist but cannot be read,[m
       [1mbash[0m reports an error.  Tildes are expanded  in  filenames  as[m
       described  below  under  [1mTilde[0m [1mExpansion[0m in the [1mEXPANSION[0m sec‚Äê[m
       tion.[m
[m
       When [1mbash[0m is invoked as an interactive login shell,  or  as  a[m
       non-interactive  shell with the [1m--login[0m option, it first reads[m
       and executes commands from the file [4m/etc/profile[24m, if that file[m
       exists.   After  reading  that file, it looks for [4m~/.bash_pro‚Äê[24m[m
       [4mfile[24m, [4m~/.bash_login[24m, and [4m~/.profile[24m, in that order, and  reads[m
       and  executes  commands  from the first one that exists and is[m
       readable.  The [1m--noprofile[0m option may be used when  the  shell[m
       is started to inhibit this behavior.[m
[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 153 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       When  an  interactive  login shell exits, or a non-interactive[m
       login shell executes the [1mexit[0m builtin command, [1mbash[0m reads  and[m
       executes commands from the file [4m~/.bash_logout[24m, if it exists.[m
[m
       When  an  interactive  shell  that  is  not  a  login shell is[m
       started,   [1mbash[0m   reads    and    executes    commands    from[m
       [4m/etc/bash.bashrc[24m  and  [4m~/.bashrc[24m,  if these files exist.  This[m
       may be inhibited by using the  [1m--norc[0m  option.   The  [1m--rcfile[0m[m
       [4mfile[24m  option will force [1mbash[0m to read and execute commands from[m
       [4mfile[24m instead of [4m/etc/bash.bashrc[24m and [4m~/.bashrc[24m.[m
[m
       When [1mbash[0m is started non-interactively, to run a shell script,[m
       for  example,  it looks for the variable [1mBASH_ENV[0m in the envi‚Äê[m
       ronment, expands its value if it appears there, and  uses  the[m
       expanded  value  as  the  name  of a file to read and execute.[m
       [1mBash[0m behaves as if the following command were executed:[m
              if [ -n "$BASH_ENV" ]; then . "$BASH_ENV"; fi[m
       but the value of the [1mPATH[0m variable is not used to  search  for[m
       the filename.[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 172 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[m
       If  [1mbash[0m  is  invoked  with the name [1msh[0m, it tries to mimic the[m
       startup behavior of historical versions of [1msh[0m  as  closely  as[m
       possible,  while  conforming  to  the  POSIX standard as well.[m
       When invoked as an interactive login shell, or a  non-interac‚Äê[m
       tive  shell with the [1m--login[0m option, it first attempts to read[m
       and execute commands from [4m/etc/profile[24m and [4m~/.profile[24m, in that[m
       order.  The [1m--noprofile[0m option may be used to inhibit this be‚Äê[m
       havior.  When invoked as an interactive shell  with  the  name[m
       [1msh[0m,  [1mbash[0m  looks for the variable [1mENV[0m, expands its value if it[m
       is defined, and uses the expanded value as the name of a  file[m
       to read and execute.  Since a shell invoked as [1msh[0m does not at‚Äê[m
       tempt to read and execute  commands  from  any  other  startup[m
       files,  the  [1m--rcfile[0m option has no effect.  A non-interactive[m
       shell invoked with the name [1msh[0m does not attempt  to  read  any[m
       other  startup  files.   When invoked as [1msh[0m, [1mbash[0m enters [4mposix[24m[m
       mode after the startup files are read.[m
[m
       When [1mbash[0m is started in [4mposix[24m mode, as with the  [1m--posix[0m  com‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 191 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       mand  line  option,  it follows the POSIX standard for startup[m
       files.  In this mode, interactive shells expand the [1mENV[0m  vari‚Äê[m
       able  and  commands  are read and executed from the file whose[m
       name is the expanded value.  No other startup files are read.[m
[m
       [1mBash[0m attempts to determine when it is being run with its stan‚Äê[m
       dard input connected to a network connection, as when executed[m
       by the historical remote shell daemon, usually  [4mrshd[24m,  or  the[m
       secure  shell daemon [4msshd[24m.  If [1mbash[0m determines it is being run[m
       non-interactively in this fashion, it reads and executes  com‚Äê[m
       mands  from [4m/etc/bash.bashrc[24m and [4m~/.bashrc[24m, if these files ex‚Äê[m
       ist and are readable.  It will not do this if invoked  as  [1msh[0m.[m
       The  [1m--norc[0m  option  may be used to inhibit this behavior, and[m
       the [1m--rcfile[0m option may be used to force another  file  to  be[m
       read,  but  neither  [4mrshd[24m  nor [4msshd[24m generally invoke the shell[m
       with those options or allow them to be specified.[m
[m
       If the shell is started with the effective user (group) id not[m
       equal  to  the  real user (group) id, and the [1m-p[0m option is not[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 210 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       supplied, no startup files are read, shell functions  are  not[m
       inherited  from  the environment, the [1mSHELLOPTS[0m, [1mBASHOPTS[0m, [1mCD‚Äê[0m[m
       [1mPATH[0m, and [1mGLOBIGNORE[0m variables, if they appear in the environ‚Äê[m
       ment,  are  ignored,  and  the effective user id is set to the[m
       real user id.  If the [1m-p[0m option is supplied at invocation, the[m
       startup behavior is the same, but the effective user id is not[m
       reset.[m
[m
[1mDEFINITIONS[0m[m
       The following definitions are used throughout the rest of this[m
       document.[m
       [1mblank[0m  A space or tab.[m
       [1mword[0m   A sequence of characters considered as a single unit by[m
              the shell.  Also known as a [1mtoken[0m.[m
       [1mname[0m   A [4mword[24m consisting only of alphanumeric  characters  and[m
              underscores, and beginning with an alphabetic character[m
              or an underscore.  Also referred to as an [1midentifier[0m.[m
       [1mmetacharacter[0m[m
              A character that, when unquoted, separates words.   One[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 229 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              of the following:[m
              [1m|[0m  [1m&[0m [1m;[0m [1m([0m [1m)[0m [1m<[0m [1m>[0m [1mspace[0m [1mtab[0m [1mnewline[0m[m
       [1mcontrol[0m [1moperator[0m[m
              A [4mtoken[24m that performs a control function.  It is one of[m
              the following symbols:[m
              [1m||[0m [1m&[0m [1m&&[0m [1m;[0m [1m;;[0m [1m;&[0m [1m;;&[0m [1m([0m [1m)[0m [1m|[0m [1m|&[0m [1m<newline>[0m[m
[m
[1mRESERVED[0m [1mWORDS[0m[m
       [4mReserved[24m [4mwords[24m are words that have a special  meaning  to  the[m
       shell.   The  following  words are recognized as reserved when[m
       unquoted and either the first word of  a  command  (see  [1mSHELL[0m[m
       [1mGRAMMAR[0m  below),  the  third  word of a [1mcase[0m or [1mselect[0m command[m
       (only [1min[0m is valid), or the third word of a [1mfor[0m  command  (only[m
       [1min[0m and [1mdo[0m are valid):[m
[m
       [1m![0m  [1mcase[0m   [1mcoproc[0m  [1mdo[0m [1mdone[0m [1melif[0m [1melse[0m [1mesac[0m [1mfi[0m [1mfor[0m [1mfunction[0m [1mif[0m [1min[0m[m
       [1mselect[0m [1mthen[0m [1muntil[0m [1mwhile[0m [1m{[0m [1m}[0m [1mtime[0m [1m[[[0m [1m]][0m[m
[m
[1mSHELL[0m [1mGRAMMAR[0m[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 248 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       This section describes the syntax  of  the  various  forms  of[m
       shell commands.[m
[m
   [1mSimple[0m [1mCommands[0m[m
       A  [4msimple[24m  [4mcommand[24m  is a sequence of optional variable assign‚Äê[m
       ments followed by [1mblank[0m-separated words and redirections,  and[m
       terminated  by  a  [4mcontrol[24m [4moperator[24m.  The first word specifies[m
       the command to be executed, and is passed  as  argument  zero.[m
       The  remaining  words  are  passed as arguments to the invoked[m
       command.[m
[m
       The return value of a [4msimple[24m [4mcommand[24m is its  exit  status,  or[m
       128+[4mn[24m if the command is terminated by signal [4mn[24m.[m
[m
   [1mPipelines[0m[m
       A  [4mpipeline[24m is a sequence of one or more commands separated by[m
       one of the control operators [1m|[0m or [1m|&[0m.  The format for a  pipe‚Äê[m
       line is:[m
[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 267 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              [[1mtime[0m [[1m-p[0m]] [ ! ] [4mcommand1[24m [ [[1m|[0m‚é™[1m|&[0m] [4mcommand2[24m ... ][m
[m
       The standard output of [4mcommand1[24m is connected via a pipe to the[m
       standard input of [4mcommand2[24m.  This connection is performed  be‚Äê[m
       fore  any redirections specified by the [4mcommand1[24m(see [1mREDIRECT‚Äê[0m[m
       [1mION[0m below).  If [1m|&[0m is used, [4mcommand1[24m's standard error, in  ad‚Äê[m
       dition  to  its  standard  output,  is connected to [4mcommand2[24m's[m
       standard input through the pipe; it is shorthand for  [1m2>&1[0m  [1m|[0m.[m
       This  implicit  redirection of the standard error to the stan‚Äê[m
       dard output is performed after any redirections  specified  by[m
       [4mcommand1[24m.[m
[m
       The return status of a pipeline is the exit status of the last[m
       command, unless the [1mpipefail[0m option is enabled.   If  [1mpipefail[0m[m
       is  enabled,  the pipeline's return status is the value of the[m
       last (rightmost) command to exit with a  non-zero  status,  or[m
       zero  if all commands exit successfully.  If the reserved word[m
       [1m![0m  precedes a pipeline, the exit status of  that  pipeline  is[m
       the  logical  negation  of the exit status as described above.[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 286 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       The shell waits for all commands in the pipeline to  terminate[m
       before returning a value.[m
[m
       If  the [1mtime[0m reserved word precedes a pipeline, the elapsed as[m
       well as user and system time consumed by its execution are re‚Äê[m
       ported  when  the  pipeline terminates.  The [1m-p[0m option changes[m
       the output format to that specified by POSIX.  When the  shell[m
       is  in  [4mposix[24m  [4mmode[24m,  it does not recognize [1mtime[0m as a reserved[m
       word if the next token begins  with  a  `-'.   The  [1mTIMEFORMAT[0m[m
       variable  may be set to a format string that specifies how the[m
       timing information should be displayed; see the description of[m
       [1mTIMEFORMAT[0m under [1mShell[0m [1mVariables[0m below.[m
[m
       When  the  shell  is  in [4mposix[24m [4mmode[24m, [1mtime[0m may be followed by a[m
       newline.  In this case, the shell displays the total user  and[m
       system time consumed by the shell and its children.  The [1mTIME‚Äê[0m[m
       [1mFORMAT[0m variable may be used to specify the format of the  time[m
       information.[m
[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 305 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       Each command in a multi-command pipeline, where pipes are cre‚Äê[m
       ated, is executed in a [4msubshell[24m, which is a separate  process.[m
       See  [1mCOMMAND[0m  [1mEXECUTION[0m  [1mENVIRONMENT[0m for a description of sub‚Äê[m
       shells and a subshell environment.  If the [1mlastpipe[0m option  is[m
       enabled  using the [1mshopt[0m builtin (see the description of [1mshopt[0m[m
       below), the last element of a pipeline may be run by the shell[m
       process when job control is not active.[m
[m
   [1mLists[0m[m
       A [4mlist[24m is a sequence of one or more pipelines separated by one[m
       of the operators [1m;[0m, [1m&[0m, [1m&&[0m, or [1m||[0m, and optionally terminated by[m
       one of [1m;[0m, [1m&[0m, or [1m<newline>[0m.[m
[m
       Of these list operators, [1m&&[0m and [1m||[0m have equal precedence, fol‚Äê[m
       lowed by [1m;[0m and [1m&[0m, which have equal precedence.[m
[m
       A sequence of one or more newlines may appear in  a  [4mlist[24m  in‚Äê[m
       stead of a semicolon to delimit commands.[m
[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 324 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       If  a  command  is  terminated  by the control operator [1m&[0m, the[m
       shell executes the command in the [4mbackground[24m  in  a  subshell.[m
       The shell does not wait for the command to finish, and the re‚Äê[m
       turn status is 0.  These are referred to as [4masynchronous[24m  com‚Äê[m
       mands.   Commands  separated by a [1m;[0m are executed sequentially;[m
       the shell waits for each command to terminate  in  turn.   The[m
       return status is the exit status of the last command executed.[m
[m
       AND  and OR lists are sequences of one or more pipelines sepa‚Äê[m
       rated by the [1m&&[0m and [1m||[0m control operators,  respectively.   AND[m
       and  OR  lists  are  executed with left associativity.  An AND[m
       list has the form[m
[m
              [4mcommand1[24m [1m&&[0m [4mcommand2[24m[m
[m
       [4mcommand2[24m is executed if, and only if, [4mcommand1[24m returns an exit[m
       status of zero (success).[m
[m
       An OR list has the form[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 343 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[m
              [4mcommand1[24m [1m||[0m [4mcommand2[24m[m
[m
       [4mcommand2[24m  is executed if, and only if, [4mcommand1[24m returns a non-[m
       zero exit status.  The return status of AND and  OR  lists  is[m
       the exit status of the last command executed in the list.[m
[m
   [1mCompound[0m [1mCommands[0m[m
       A  [4mcompound[24m  [4mcommand[24m is one of the following.  In most cases a[m
       [4mlist[24m in a command's description may be separated from the rest[m
       of the command by one or more newlines, and may be followed by[m
       a newline in place of a semicolon.[m
[m
       ([4mlist[24m) [4mlist[24m is executed in a subshell (see  [1mCOMMAND[0m  [1mEXECUTION[0m[m
              [1mENVIRONMENT[0m below for a description of a subshell envi‚Äê[m
              ronment).  Variable assignments  and  builtin  commands[m
              that  affect  the  shell's environment do not remain in[m
              effect after the command completes.  The return  status[m
              is the exit status of [4mlist[24m.[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 362 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[m
       { [4mlist[24m; }[m
              [4mlist[24m  is  simply executed in the current shell environ‚Äê[m
              ment.  [4mlist[24m must be terminated with a newline or  semi‚Äê[m
              colon.   This  is known as a [4mgroup[24m [4mcommand[24m.  The return[m
              status is the exit status of [4mlist[24m.   Note  that  unlike[m
              the  metacharacters [1m([0m and [1m)[0m, [1m{[0m and [1m}[0m are [4mreserved[24m [4mwords[24m[m
              and must occur where a reserved word is permitted to be[m
              recognized.  Since they do not cause a word break, they[m
              must be separated from [4mlist[24m by  whitespace  or  another[m
              shell metacharacter.[m
[m
       (([4mexpression[24m))[m
              The  [4mexpression[24m is evaluated according to the rules de‚Äê[m
              scribed below  under  [1mARITHMETIC[0m  [1mEVALUATION[0m.   If  the[m
              value  of the expression is non-zero, the return status[m
              is 0; otherwise the return status is 1.  The [4mexpression[24m[m
              undergoes the same expansions as if it were within dou‚Äê[m
              ble quotes, but double quote characters  in  [4mexpression[24m[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 381 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              are not treated specially and are removed.[m
[m
       [1m[[[0m [4mexpression[24m [1m]][0m[m
              Return  a  status of 0 or 1 depending on the evaluation[m
              of the conditional expression [4mexpression[24m.   Expressions[m
              are  composed  of  the  primaries described below under[m
              [1mCONDITIONAL[0m [1mEXPRESSIONS[0m.  The words between the [1m[[[0m  and[m
              [1m]][0m  do  not  undergo word splitting and pathname expan‚Äê[m
              sion.  The shell performs  tilde  expansion,  parameter[m
              and  variable  expansion, arithmetic expansion, command[m
              substitution, process substitution, and  quote  removal[m
              on  those words (the expansions that would occur if the[m
              words were enclosed in double quotes).  Conditional op‚Äê[m
              erators such as [1m-f[0m must be unquoted to be recognized as[m
              primaries.[m
[m
              When used with [1m[[[0m, the [1m<[0m and [1m>[0m operators  sort  lexico‚Äê[m
              graphically using the current locale.[m
[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 400 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       See the description of the [4mtest[24m builtin command (section SHELL[m
       BUILTIN COMMANDS below) for the handling of  parameters  (i.e.[m
       missing parameters).[m
[m
       When the [1m==[0m and [1m!=[0m operators are used, the string to the right[m
       of the operator is considered a pattern and matched  according[m
       to the rules described below under [1mPattern[0m [1mMatching[0m, as if the[m
       [1mextglob[0m shell option were enabled.  The [1m=[0m operator is  equiva‚Äê[m
       lent  to  [1m==[0m.  If the [1mnocasematch[0m shell option is enabled, the[m
       match is performed without regard to the  case  of  alphabetic[m
       characters.   The return value is 0 if the string matches ([1m==[0m)[m
       or does not match ([1m!=[0m) the pattern, and 1 otherwise.  Any part[m
       of the pattern may be quoted to force the quoted portion to be[m
       matched as a string.[m
[m
       An additional binary operator, [1m=~[0m, is available, with the same[m
       precedence  as  [1m==[0m and [1m!=[0m.  When it is used, the string to the[m
       right of the operator is considered a POSIX  extended  regular[m
       expression  and  matched  accordingly (using the POSIX [4mregcomp[24m[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 419 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       and [4mregexec[24m interfaces usually described  in  [4mregex[24m(3)).   The[m
       return  value  is  0  if the string matches the pattern, and 1[m
       otherwise.  If the regular expression is syntactically  incor‚Äê[m
       rect,  the conditional expression's return value is 2.  If the[m
       [1mnocasematch[0m shell option is enabled, the  match  is  performed[m
       without  regard  to the case of alphabetic characters.  If any[m
       part of the pattern is quoted, the quoted portion  is  matched[m
       literally.   This  means every character in the quoted portion[m
       matches itself, instead of having any special pattern matching[m
       meaning.   If the pattern is stored in a shell variable, quot‚Äê[m
       ing the variable expansion forces the  entire  pattern  to  be[m
       matched  literally.   Treat bracket expressions in regular ex‚Äê[m
       pressions carefully, since normal quoting and pattern  charac‚Äê[m
       ters lose their meanings between brackets.[m
[m
       The  pattern  will match if it matches any part of the string.[m
       Anchor the pattern using the [1m^[0m and [1m$[0m regular expression opera‚Äê[m
       tors  to force it to match the entire string.  The array vari‚Äê[m
       able [1mBASH_REMATCH[0m records which parts of  the  string  matched[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 438 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       the  pattern.   The  element of [1mBASH_REMATCH[0m with index 0 con‚Äê[m
       tains the portion of the string matching  the  entire  regular[m
       expression.   Substrings  matched  by parenthesized subexpres‚Äê[m
       sions within the regular expression are saved in the remaining[m
       [1mBASH_REMATCH[0m indices. The element of [1mBASH_REMATCH[0m with index [4mn[24m[m
       is the portion of the string matching  the  [4mn[24mth  parenthesized[m
       subexpression.   Bash  sets  [1mBASH_REMATCH[0m in the global scope;[m
       declaring it as a local variable will lead to  unexpected  re‚Äê[m
       sults.[m
[m
       Expressions  may  be  combined  using the following operators,[m
       listed in decreasing order of precedence:[m
[m
              [1m([0m [4mexpression[24m [1m)[0m[m
                     Returns the value of [4mexpression[24m.   This  may  be[m
                     used to override the normal precedence of opera‚Äê[m
                     tors.[m
              [1m![0m [4mexpression[24m[m
                     True if [4mexpression[24m is false.[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 457 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              [4mexpression1[24m [1m&&[0m [4mexpression2[24m[m
                     True if both  [4mexpression1[24m  and  [4mexpression2[24m  are[m
                     true.[m
              [4mexpression1[24m [1m||[0m [4mexpression2[24m[m
                     True  if  either  [4mexpression1[24m  or [4mexpression2[24m is[m
                     true.[m
[m
              The [1m&&[0m and [1m||[0m operators do not evaluate [4mexpression2[24m  if[m
              the value of [4mexpression1[24m is sufficient to determine the[m
              return value of the entire conditional expression.[m

       [1mfor[0m [4mname[24m [ [ [1min[0m [ [4mword[24m [4m...[24m ] ] ; ] [1mdo[0m [4mlist[24m ; [1mdone[0m[m
              The list of words following [1min[0m is expanded,  generating[m
              a list of items.  The variable [4mname[24m is set to each ele‚Äê[m
              ment of this list in turn, and [4mlist[24m  is  executed  each[m

              set  (see  [1mPARAMETERS[0m below).  The return status is the[m

[7m Manual page bash(1) line 476 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              expansion of the items following [1min[0m results in an empty[m

       [1mfor[0m (( [4mexpr1[24m ; [4mexpr2[24m ; [4mexpr3[24m )) ; [1mdo[0m [4mlist[24m ; [1mdone[0m[m

[?2004lset: set [-abefhkmnptuvxBCEHPT] [-o option-name] [--] [-] [arg ...]
    Set or unset values of shell options and positional parameters.
    
    Change the value of shell attributes and positional parameters, or
    display the names and values of shell variables.
    
    Options:
      -a  Mark variables which are modified or created for export.
      -b  Notify of job termination immediately.
      -e  Exit immediately if a command exits with a non-zero status.
      -f  Disable file name generation (globbing).
      -h  Remember the location of commands as they are looked up.
      -k  All assignment arguments are placed in the environment for a
          command, not just those that precede the command name.
      -m  Job control is enabled.
      -n  Read commands but do not execute them.
      -o option-name
          Set the variable corresponding to option-name:
              allexport    same as -a
              braceexpand  same as -B
              emacs        use an emacs-style line editing interface
              errexit      same as -e
              errtrace     same as -E
              functrace    same as -T
              hashall      same as -h
              histexpand   same as -H
              history      enable command history
              ignoreeof    the shell will not exit upon reading EOF
              interactive-comments
                           allow comments to appear in interactive commands
              keyword      same as -k
              monitor      same as -m
              noclobber    same as -C
              noexec       same as -n
              noglob       same as -f
              nolog        currently accepted but ignored
              notify       same as -b
              nounset      same as -u
              onecmd       same as -t
              physical     same as -P
              pipefail     the return value of a pipeline is the status of
                           the last command to exit with a non-zero status,
                           or zero if no command exited with a non-zero status
              posix        change the behavior of bash where the default
                           operation differs from the Posix standard to
                           match the standard
              privileged   same as -p
              verbose      same as -v
              vi           use a vi-style line editing interface
              xtrace       same as -x
      -p  Turned on whenever the real and effective user ids do not match.
          Disables processing of the $ENV file and importing of shell
          functions.  Turning this option off causes the effective uid and
          gid to be set to the real uid and gid.
      -t  Exit after reading and executing one command.
      -u  Treat unset variables as an error when substituting.
      -v  Print shell input lines as they are read.
      -x  Print commands and their arguments as they are executed.
      -B  the shell will perform brace expansion
      -C  If set, disallow existing regular files to be overwritten
          by redirection of output.
      -E  If set, the ERR trap is inherited by shell functions.
      -H  Enable ! style history substitution.  This flag is on
          by default when the shell is interactive.
      -P  If set, do not resolve symbolic links when executing commands
          such as cd which change the current directory.
      -T  If set, the DEBUG and RETURN traps are inherited by shell functions.
      --  Assign any remaining arguments to the positional parameters.
          If there are no remaining arguments, the positional parameters
          are unset.
      -   Assign any remaining arguments to the positional parameters.
          The -x and -v options are turned off.
    
    Using + rather than - causes these flags to be turned off.  The
    flags can also be used upon invocation of the shell.  The current
    set of flags may be found in $-.  The remaining n ARGs are positional
    parameters and are assigned, in order, to $1, $2, .. $n.  If no
    ARGs are given, all shell variables are printed.
    
    Exit Status:
    Returns success unless an invalid option is given.

[?2004l[?1049h[22;0;0t[?1h=BASH(1)                General Commands Manual                BASH(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       bash - GNU Bourne-Again SHell[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mbash[0m [options] [command_string | file][m
[m
[1mCOPYRIGHT[0m[m
       Bash  is  Copyright (C) 1989-2022 by the Free Software Founda‚Äê[m
       tion, Inc.[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mBash[0m is an [1msh[0m-compatible command language interpreter that ex‚Äê[m
       ecutes  commands  read from the standard input or from a file.[m
       [1mBash[0m also incorporates useful features from  the  [4mKorn[24m  and  [4mC[24m[m
       shells ([1mksh[0m and [1mcsh[0m).[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K[[[K[[[K[K[7mInvalid pattern  (press RETURN)[27m[18;1H[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 2 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       [1mBash[0m  is  intended  to  be  a conformant implementation of the[m
       Shell and Utilities portion of the  IEEE  POSIX  specification[m
       (IEEE  Standard  1003.1).  [1mBash[0m can be configured to be POSIX-[m
       conformant by default.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       All of the single-character shell options  documented  in  the[m
       description  of  the [1mset[0m builtin command, including [1m-o[0m, can be[m
       used as options when the shell is invoked.  In addition,  [1mbash[0m[m
       interprets the following options when it is invoked:[m
[m
       [1m-c[0m        If  the [1m-c[0m option is present, then commands are read[m
                 from the first non-option  argument  [4mcommand_string[24m.[m
                 If there are arguments after the [4mcommand_string[24m, the[m
                 first argument is assigned to [1m$0[0m and  any  remaining[m
                 arguments are assigned to the positional parameters.[m
                 The assignment to [1m$0[0m sets the  name  of  the  shell,[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 19 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K                 which is used in warning and error messages.[m
       [1m-i[0m        If  the  [1m-i[0m option is present, the shell is [4minterac‚Äê[24m[m
                 [4mtive[24m.[m
       [1m-l[0m        Make [1mbash[0m act as if it had been invoked as  a  login[m
                 shell (see [1mINVOCATION[0m below).[m
       [1m-r[0m        If  the  [1m-r[0m option is present, the shell becomes [4mre‚Äê[24m[m
                 [4mstricted[24m (see [1mRESTRICTED[0m [1mSHELL[0m below).[m
       [1m-s[0m        If the [1m-s[0m option is present, or if no arguments  re‚Äê[m
                 main after option processing, then commands are read[m
                 from the standard input.  This option allows the po‚Äê[m
                 sitional  parameters  to be set when invoking an in‚Äê[m
                 teractive shell or  when  reading  input  through  a[m
                 pipe.[m
       [1m-v[0m        Print shell input lines as they are read.[m
       [1m-x[0m        Print  commands and their arguments as they are exe‚Äê[m
                 cuted.[m
       [1m-D[0m        A list of all double-quoted strings preceded by [1m$[0m is[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 36 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K                 printed  on  the  standard  output.   These  are the[m
                 strings that are  subject  to  language  translation[m
                 when the current locale is not [1mC[0m or [1mPOSIX[0m.  This im‚Äê[m
                 plies the [1m-n[0m option; no commands will be executed.[m
       [1m[-+]O[0m [1m[[0m[4mshopt_option[24m[1m][0m[m
                 [4mshopt_option[24m is one of the shell options accepted by[m
                 the  [1mshopt[0m  builtin  (see [1mSHELL[0m [1mBUILTIN[0m [1mCOMMANDS[0m be‚Äê[m
                 low).  If [4mshopt_option[24m is present, [1m-O[0m sets the value[m
                 of  that  option;  [1m+O[0m unsets it.  If [4mshopt_option[24m is[m
                 not supplied, the names and values of the shell  op‚Äê[m
                 tions  accepted by [1mshopt[0m are printed on the standard[m
                 output.  If the invocation option is [1m+O[0m, the  output[m
                 is  displayed  in a format that may be reused as in‚Äê[m
                 put.[m
       [1m--[0m        A [1m--[0m signals the end of options and disables further[m
                 option  processing.   Any arguments after the [1m--[0m are[m
                 treated as filenames and arguments.  An argument  of[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 53 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K                 [1m-[0m is equivalent to [1m--[0m.[m
[m
       [1mBash[0m  also  interprets  a  number  of multi-character options.[m
       These options must appear on the command line before the  sin‚Äê[m
       gle-character options to be recognized.[m
[m
       [1m--debugger[0m[m
              Arrange  for the debugger profile to be executed before[m
              the shell starts.  Turns  on  extended  debugging  mode[m
              (see  the  description  of  the  [1mextdebug[0m option to the[m
              [1mshopt[0m builtin below).[m
       [1m--dump-po-strings[0m[m
              Equivalent to [1m-D[0m, but the output is in the GNU  [4mgettext[24m[m
              [1mpo[0m (portable object) file format.[m
       [1m--dump-strings[0m[m
              Equivalent to [1m-D[0m.[m
       [1m--help[0m Display  a  usage  message  on standard output and exit[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 70 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              successfully.[m
       [1m--init-file[0m [4mfile[24m[m
       [1m--rcfile[0m [4mfile[24m[m
              Execute commands from [4mfile[24m instead of the  system  wide[m
              initialization  file  [4m/etc/bash.bashrc[24m and the standard[m
              personal initialization file [4m~/.bashrc[24m if the shell  is[m
              interactive (see [1mINVOCATION[0m below).[m
[m
       [1m--login[0m[m
              Equivalent to [1m-l[0m.[m
[m
       [1m--noediting[0m[m
              Do  not  use  the  GNU [1mreadline[0m library to read command[m
              lines when the shell is interactive.[m
[m
       [1m--noprofile[0m[m
              Do  not  read  either  the  system-wide  startup   file[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 87 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              [4m/etc/profile[24m  or  any  of  the  personal initialization[m
              files [4m~/.bash_profile[24m,  [4m~/.bash_login[24m,  or  [4m~/.profile[24m.[m
              By  default,  [1mbash[0m reads these files when it is invoked[m
              as a login shell (see [1mINVOCATION[0m below).[m
[m
       [1m--norc[0m Do not read and execute the system wide  initialization[m
              file  [4m/etc/bash.bashrc[24m  and the personal initialization[m
              file [4m~/.bashrc[24m if the shell is interactive.   This  op‚Äê[m
              tion is on by default if the shell is invoked as [1msh[0m.[m
[m
       [1m--posix[0m[m
              Change the behavior of [1mbash[0m where the default operation[m
              differs from the POSIX standard to match  the  standard[m
              ([4mposix[24m  [4mmode[24m).  See [1mSEE[0m [1mALSO[0m below for a reference to a[m
              document that details how posix mode affects bash's be‚Äê[m
              havior.[m
[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 104 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       [1m--restricted[0m[m
              The  shell becomes restricted (see [1mRESTRICTED[0m [1mSHELL[0m be‚Äê[m
              low).[m
[m
       [1m--verbose[0m[m
              Equivalent to [1m-v[0m.[m
[m
       [1m--version[0m[m
              Show version information for this instance of  [1mbash[0m  on[m
              the standard output and exit successfully.[m
[m
[1mARGUMENTS[0m[m
       If  arguments  remain after option processing, and neither the[m
       [1m-c[0m nor the [1m-s[0m option has been supplied, the first argument  is[m
       assumed  to  be  the name of a file containing shell commands.[m
       If [1mbash[0m is invoked in this fashion, [1m$0[0m is set to the  name  of[m
       the file, and the positional parameters are set to the remain‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 121 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       ing arguments.  [1mBash[0m reads and  executes  commands  from  this[m
       file,  then  exits.   [1mBash[0m's exit status is the exit status of[m
       the last command executed in the script.  If no  commands  are[m
       executed,  the  exit status is 0.  An attempt is first made to[m
       open the file in the current directory, and,  if  no  file  is[m
       found, then the shell searches the directories in [1mPATH[0m for the[m
       script.[m
[m
[1mINVOCATION[0m[m
       A [4mlogin[24m [4mshell[24m is one whose first character of argument zero is[m
       a [1m-[0m, or one started with the [1m--login[0m option.[m
[m
       An  [4minteractive[24m  shell is one started without non-option argu‚Äê[m
       ments (unless [1m-s[0m is specified)  and  without  the  [1m-c[0m  option,[m
       whose standard input and error are both connected to terminals[m
       (as determined by [4misatty[24m(3)), or one started with the  [1m-i[0m  op‚Äê[m
       tion.   [1mPS1[0m  is  set and [1m$-[0m includes [1mi[0m if [1mbash[0m is interactive,[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 138 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       allowing a shell script or a startup file to test this state.[m
[m
       The  following  paragraphs  describe  how  [1mbash[0m  executes  its[m
       startup  files.  If any of the files exist but cannot be read,[m
       [1mbash[0m reports an error.  Tildes are expanded  in  filenames  as[m
       described  below  under  [1mTilde[0m [1mExpansion[0m in the [1mEXPANSION[0m sec‚Äê[m
       tion.[m
[m
       When [1mbash[0m is invoked as an interactive login shell,  or  as  a[m
       non-interactive  shell with the [1m--login[0m option, it first reads[m
       and executes commands from the file [4m/etc/profile[24m, if that file[m
       exists.   After  reading  that file, it looks for [4m~/.bash_pro‚Äê[24m[m
       [4mfile[24m, [4m~/.bash_login[24m, and [4m~/.profile[24m, in that order, and  reads[m
       and  executes  commands  from the first one that exists and is[m
       readable.  The [1m--noprofile[0m option may be used when  the  shell[m
       is started to inhibit this behavior.[m
[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 155 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       When  an  interactive  login shell exits, or a non-interactive[m
       login shell executes the [1mexit[0m builtin command, [1mbash[0m reads  and[m
       executes commands from the file [4m~/.bash_logout[24m, if it exists.[m
[m
       When  an  interactive  shell  that  is  not  a  login shell is[m
       started,   [1mbash[0m   reads    and    executes    commands    from[m
       [4m/etc/bash.bashrc[24m  and  [4m~/.bashrc[24m,  if these files exist.  This[m
       may be inhibited by using the  [1m--norc[0m  option.   The  [1m--rcfile[0m[m
       [4mfile[24m  option will force [1mbash[0m to read and execute commands from[m
       [4mfile[24m instead of [4m/etc/bash.bashrc[24m and [4m~/.bashrc[24m.[m
[m
       When [1mbash[0m is started non-interactively, to run a shell script,[m
       for  example,  it looks for the variable [1mBASH_ENV[0m in the envi‚Äê[m
       ronment, expands its value if it appears there, and  uses  the[m
       expanded  value  as  the  name  of a file to read and execute.[m
       [1mBash[0m behaves as if the following command were executed:[m
              if [ -n "$BASH_ENV" ]; then . "$BASH_ENV"; fi[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 172 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       but the value of the [1mPATH[0m variable is not used to  search  for[m
       the filename.[m
[m
       If  [1mbash[0m  is  invoked  with the name [1msh[0m, it tries to mimic the[m
       startup behavior of historical versions of [1msh[0m  as  closely  as[m
       possible,  while  conforming  to  the  POSIX standard as well.[m
       When invoked as an interactive login shell, or a  non-interac‚Äê[m
       tive  shell with the [1m--login[0m option, it first attempts to read[m
       and execute commands from [4m/etc/profile[24m and [4m~/.profile[24m, in that[m
       order.  The [1m--noprofile[0m option may be used to inhibit this be‚Äê[m
       havior.  When invoked as an interactive shell  with  the  name[m
       [1msh[0m,  [1mbash[0m  looks for the variable [1mENV[0m, expands its value if it[m
       is defined, and uses the expanded value as the name of a  file[m
       to read and execute.  Since a shell invoked as [1msh[0m does not at‚Äê[m
       tempt to read and execute  commands  from  any  other  startup[m
       files,  the  [1m--rcfile[0m option has no effect.  A non-interactive[m
       shell invoked with the name [1msh[0m does not attempt  to  read  any[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 189 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       other  startup  files.   When invoked as [1msh[0m, [1mbash[0m enters [4mposix[24m[m
       mode after the startup files are read.[m
[m
       When [1mbash[0m is started in [4mposix[24m mode, as with the  [1m--posix[0m  com‚Äê[m
       mand  line  option,  it follows the POSIX standard for startup[m
       files.  In this mode, interactive shells expand the [1mENV[0m  vari‚Äê[m
       able  and  commands  are read and executed from the file whose[m
       name is the expanded value.  No other startup files are read.[m
[m
       [1mBash[0m attempts to determine when it is being run with its stan‚Äê[m
       dard input connected to a network connection, as when executed[m
       by the historical remote shell daemon, usually  [4mrshd[24m,  or  the[m
       secure  shell daemon [4msshd[24m.  If [1mbash[0m determines it is being run[m
       non-interactively in this fashion, it reads and executes  com‚Äê[m
       mands  from [4m/etc/bash.bashrc[24m and [4m~/.bashrc[24m, if these files ex‚Äê[m
       ist and are readable.  It will not do this if invoked  as  [1msh[0m.[m
       The  [1m--norc[0m  option  may be used to inhibit this behavior, and[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 206 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       the [1m--rcfile[0m option may be used to force another  file  to  be[m
       read,  but  neither  [4mrshd[24m  nor [4msshd[24m generally invoke the shell[m
       with those options or allow them to be specified.[m
[m
       If the shell is started with the effective user (group) id not[m
       equal  to  the  real user (group) id, and the [1m-p[0m option is not[m
       supplied, no startup files are read, shell functions  are  not[m
       inherited  from  the environment, the [1mSHELLOPTS[0m, [1mBASHOPTS[0m, [1mCD‚Äê[0m[m
       [1mPATH[0m, and [1mGLOBIGNORE[0m variables, if they appear in the environ‚Äê[m
       ment,  are  ignored,  and  the effective user id is set to the[m
       real user id.  If the [1m-p[0m option is supplied at invocation, the[m
       startup behavior is the same, but the effective user id is not[m
       reset.[m
[m
[1mDEFINITIONS[0m[m
       The following definitions are used throughout the rest of this[m
       document.[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 223 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       [1mblank[0m  A space or tab.[m
       [1mword[0m   A sequence of characters considered as a single unit by[m
              the shell.  Also known as a [1mtoken[0m.[m
       [1mname[0m   A [4mword[24m consisting only of alphanumeric  characters  and[m
              underscores, and beginning with an alphabetic character[m
              or an underscore.  Also referred to as an [1midentifier[0m.[m
       [1mmetacharacter[0m[m
              A character that, when unquoted, separates words.   One[m
              of the following:[m
              [1m|[0m  [1m&[0m [1m;[0m [1m([0m [1m)[0m [1m<[0m [1m>[0m [1mspace[0m [1mtab[0m [1mnewline[0m[m
       [1mcontrol[0m [1moperator[0m[m
              A [4mtoken[24m that performs a control function.  It is one of[m
              the following symbols:[m
              [1m||[0m [1m&[0m [1m&&[0m [1m;[0m [1m;;[0m [1m;&[0m [1m;;&[0m [1m([0m [1m)[0m [1m|[0m [1m|&[0m [1m<newline>[0m[m
[m
[1mRESERVED[0m [1mWORDS[0m[m
       [4mReserved[24m [4mwords[24m are words that have a special  meaning  to  the[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 240 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       shell.   The  following  words are recognized as reserved when[m
       unquoted and either the first word of  a  command  (see  [1mSHELL[0m[m
       [1mGRAMMAR[0m  below),  the  third  word of a [1mcase[0m or [1mselect[0m command[m
       (only [1min[0m is valid), or the third word of a [1mfor[0m  command  (only[m
       [1min[0m and [1mdo[0m are valid):[m
[m
       [1m![0m  [1mcase[0m   [1mcoproc[0m  [1mdo[0m [1mdone[0m [1melif[0m [1melse[0m [1mesac[0m [1mfi[0m [1mfor[0m [1mfunction[0m [1mif[0m [1min[0m[m
       [1mselect[0m [1mthen[0m [1muntil[0m [1mwhile[0m [1m{[0m [1m}[0m [1mtime[0m [1m[[[0m [1m]][0m[m
[m
[1mSHELL[0m [1mGRAMMAR[0m[m
       This section describes the syntax  of  the  various  forms  of[m
       shell commands.[m
[m
   [1mSimple[0m [1mCommands[0m[m
       A  [4msimple[24m  [4mcommand[24m  is a sequence of optional variable assign‚Äê[m
       ments followed by [1mblank[0m-separated words and redirections,  and[m
       terminated  by  a  [4mcontrol[24m [4moperator[24m.  The first word specifies[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 257 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       the command to be executed, and is passed  as  argument  zero.[m
       The  remaining  words  are  passed as arguments to the invoked[m
       command.[m
[m
       The return value of a [4msimple[24m [4mcommand[24m is its  exit  status,  or[m
       128+[4mn[24m if the command is terminated by signal [4mn[24m.[m
[m
   [1mPipelines[0m[m
       A  [4mpipeline[24m is a sequence of one or more commands separated by[m
       one of the control operators [1m|[0m or [1m|&[0m.  The format for a  pipe‚Äê[m
       line is:[m
[m
              [[1mtime[0m [[1m-p[0m]] [ ! ] [4mcommand1[24m [ [[1m|[0m‚é™[1m|&[0m] [4mcommand2[24m ... ][m
[m
       The standard output of [4mcommand1[24m is connected via a pipe to the[m
       standard input of [4mcommand2[24m.  This connection is performed  be‚Äê[m
       fore  any redirections specified by the [4mcommand1[24m(see [1mREDIRECT‚Äê[0m[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 274 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       [1mION[0m below).  If [1m|&[0m is used, [4mcommand1[24m's standard error, in  ad‚Äê[m
       dition  to  its  standard  output,  is connected to [4mcommand2[24m's[m
       standard input through the pipe; it is shorthand for  [1m2>&1[0m  [1m|[0m.[m
       This  implicit  redirection of the standard error to the stan‚Äê[m
       dard output is performed after any redirections  specified  by[m
       [4mcommand1[24m.[m
[m
       The return status of a pipeline is the exit status of the last[m
       command, unless the [1mpipefail[0m option is enabled.   If  [1mpipefail[0m[m
       is  enabled,  the pipeline's return status is the value of the[m
       last (rightmost) command to exit with a  non-zero  status,  or[m
       zero  if all commands exit successfully.  If the reserved word[m
       [1m![0m  precedes a pipeline, the exit status of  that  pipeline  is[m
       the  logical  negation  of the exit status as described above.[m
       The shell waits for all commands in the pipeline to  terminate[m
       before returning a value.[m
[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 291 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       If  the [1mtime[0m reserved word precedes a pipeline, the elapsed as[m
       well as user and system time consumed by its execution are re‚Äê[m
       ported  when  the  pipeline terminates.  The [1m-p[0m option changes[m
       the output format to that specified by POSIX.  When the  shell[m
       is  in  [4mposix[24m  [4mmode[24m,  it does not recognize [1mtime[0m as a reserved[m
       word if the next token begins  with  a  `-'.   The  [1mTIMEFORMAT[0m[m
       variable  may be set to a format string that specifies how the[m
       timing information should be displayed; see the description of[m
       [1mTIMEFORMAT[0m under [1mShell[0m [1mVariables[0m below.[m
[m
       When  the  shell  is  in [4mposix[24m [4mmode[24m, [1mtime[0m may be followed by a[m
       newline.  In this case, the shell displays the total user  and[m
       system time consumed by the shell and its children.  The [1mTIME‚Äê[0m[m
       [1mFORMAT[0m variable may be used to specify the format of the  time[m
       information.[m
[m
       Each command in a multi-command pipeline, where pipes are cre‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 308 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       ated, is executed in a [4msubshell[24m, which is a separate  process.[m
       See  [1mCOMMAND[0m  [1mEXECUTION[0m  [1mENVIRONMENT[0m for a description of sub‚Äê[m
       shells and a subshell environment.  If the [1mlastpipe[0m option  is[m
       enabled  using the [1mshopt[0m builtin (see the description of [1mshopt[0m[m
       below), the last element of a pipeline may be run by the shell[m
       process when job control is not active.[m
[m
   [1mLists[0m[m
       A [4mlist[24m is a sequence of one or more pipelines separated by one[m
       of the operators [1m;[0m, [1m&[0m, [1m&&[0m, or [1m||[0m, and optionally terminated by[m
       one of [1m;[0m, [1m&[0m, or [1m<newline>[0m.[m
[m
       Of these list operators, [1m&&[0m and [1m||[0m have equal precedence, fol‚Äê[m
       lowed by [1m;[0m and [1m&[0m, which have equal precedence.[m
[m
       A sequence of one or more newlines may appear in  a  [4mlist[24m  in‚Äê[m
       stead of a semicolon to delimit commands.[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 325 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[m
       If  a  command  is  terminated  by the control operator [1m&[0m, the[m
       shell executes the command in the [4mbackground[24m  in  a  subshell.[m
       The shell does not wait for the command to finish, and the re‚Äê[m
       turn status is 0.  These are referred to as [4masynchronous[24m  com‚Äê[m
       mands.   Commands  separated by a [1m;[0m are executed sequentially;[m
       the shell waits for each command to terminate  in  turn.   The[m
       return status is the exit status of the last command executed.[m
[m
       AND  and OR lists are sequences of one or more pipelines sepa‚Äê[m
       rated by the [1m&&[0m and [1m||[0m control operators,  respectively.   AND[m
       and  OR  lists  are  executed with left associativity.  An AND[m
       list has the form[m
[m
              [4mcommand1[24m [1m&&[0m [4mcommand2[24m[m
[m
       [4mcommand2[24m is executed if, and only if, [4mcommand1[24m returns an exit[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 342 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       status of zero (success).[m
[m
       An OR list has the form[m
[m
              [4mcommand1[24m [1m||[0m [4mcommand2[24m[m
[m
       [4mcommand2[24m  is executed if, and only if, [4mcommand1[24m returns a non-[m
       zero exit status.  The return status of AND and  OR  lists  is[m
       the exit status of the last command executed in the list.[m
[m
   [1mCompound[0m [1mCommands[0m[m
       A  [4mcompound[24m  [4mcommand[24m is one of the following.  In most cases a[m
       [4mlist[24m in a command's description may be separated from the rest[m
       of the command by one or more newlines, and may be followed by[m
       a newline in place of a semicolon.[m
[m
       ([4mlist[24m) [4mlist[24m is executed in a subshell (see  [1mCOMMAND[0m  [1mEXECUTION[0m[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 359 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              [1mENVIRONMENT[0m below for a description of a subshell envi‚Äê[m
              ronment).  Variable assignments  and  builtin  commands[m
              that  affect  the  shell's environment do not remain in[m
              effect after the command completes.  The return  status[m
              is the exit status of [4mlist[24m.[m
[m
       { [4mlist[24m; }[m
              [4mlist[24m  is  simply executed in the current shell environ‚Äê[m
              ment.  [4mlist[24m must be terminated with a newline or  semi‚Äê[m
              colon.   This  is known as a [4mgroup[24m [4mcommand[24m.  The return[m
              status is the exit status of [4mlist[24m.   Note  that  unlike[m
              the  metacharacters [1m([0m and [1m)[0m, [1m{[0m and [1m}[0m are [4mreserved[24m [4mwords[24m[m
              and must occur where a reserved word is permitted to be[m
              recognized.  Since they do not cause a word break, they[m
              must be separated from [4mlist[24m by  whitespace  or  another[m
              shell metacharacter.[m
[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 376 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       (([4mexpression[24m))[m
              The  [4mexpression[24m is evaluated according to the rules de‚Äê[m
              scribed below  under  [1mARITHMETIC[0m  [1mEVALUATION[0m.   If  the[m
              value  of the expression is non-zero, the return status[m
              is 0; otherwise the return status is 1.  The [4mexpression[24m[m
              undergoes the same expansions as if it were within dou‚Äê[m
              ble quotes, but double quote characters  in  [4mexpression[24m[m
              are not treated specially and are removed.[m
[m
       [1m[[[0m [4mexpression[24m [1m]][0m[m
              Return  a  status of 0 or 1 depending on the evaluation[m
              of the conditional expression [4mexpression[24m.   Expressions[m
              are  composed  of  the  primaries described below under[m
              [1mCONDITIONAL[0m [1mEXPRESSIONS[0m.  The words between the [1m[[[0m  and[m
              [1m]][0m  do  not  undergo word splitting and pathname expan‚Äê[m
              sion.  The shell performs  tilde  expansion,  parameter[m
              and  variable  expansion, arithmetic expansion, command[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 393 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM[m
[18;1H[K[7m Manual page bash(1) line 392 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM              shell metacharacter.[m
[18;1H[K[7m Manual page bash(1) line 391 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM              must be separated from [4mlist[24m by  whitespace  or  another[m
[18;1H[K[7m Manual page bash(1) line 390 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM              recognized.  Since they do not cause a word break, they[m
[18;1H[K[7m Manual page bash(1) line 389 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM              and must occur where a reserved word is permitted to be[m
[18;1H[K[7m Manual page bash(1) line 388 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM              the  metacharacters [1m([0m and [1m)[0m, [1m{[0m and [1m}[0m are [4mreserved[24m [4mwords[24m[m
[18;1H[K[7m Manual page bash(1) line 387 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM              status is the exit status of [4mlist[24m.   Note  that  unlike[m
[18;1H[K[7m Manual page bash(1) line 386 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM              colon.   This  is known as a [4mgroup[24m [4mcommand[24m.  The return[m
[18;1H[K[7m Manual page bash(1) line 385 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM              ment.  [4mlist[24m must be terminated with a newline or  semi‚Äê[m
[18;1H[K[7m Manual page bash(1) line 384 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM              [4mlist[24m  is  simply executed in the current shell environ‚Äê[m
[18;1H[K[7m Manual page bash(1) line 383 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM       { [4mlist[24m; }[m
[18;1H[K[7m Manual page bash(1) line 382 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM[m
[18;1H[K[7m Manual page bash(1) line 381 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM              is the exit status of [4mlist[24m.[m
[18;1H[K[7m Manual page bash(1) line 380 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM              effect after the command completes.  The return  status[m
[18;1H[K[7m Manual page bash(1) line 379 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[HM              that  affect  the  shell's environment do not remain in[m
[18;1H[K[7m Manual page bash(1) line 378 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              scribed below  under  [1mARITHMETIC[0m  [1mEVALUATION[0m.   If  the[m
